<div id="review_18190030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18190030" />
    <a title="CJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1008029-cj"><img alt="CJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222819434p2/1008029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18190030?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CJ" href="/user/show/1008029-cj">CJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18190030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer190724410658000724">Best of the series - this book takes a closer look at Edward and his world. Anita makes some surprising and frightening discoveries about the mystery man in her life. <br/> If you were ready for a break from the vampire politics,the hot and heavy romance and the soul searching that came with said romance, this book is for you. <br/> This is the first step in the author's contention that the real monsters are not always the ones with fangs and super human powers, and she presents this with a skillful subtl</span>
  <span id="freeText190724410658000724" style="display:none">Best of the series - this book takes a closer look at Edward and his world. Anita makes some surprising and frightening discoveries about the mystery man in her life. <br /> If you were ready for a break from the vampire politics,the hot and heavy romance and the soul searching that came with said romance, this book is for you. <br /> This is the first step in the author's contention that the real monsters are not always the ones with fangs and super human powers, and she presents this with a skillful subtlety that vanishes later in the series. <br /> I thought Laurell K Hamilton was a solidly good writer until this book; after this book, I thought she was a gifted writer. <br /> The books that come after Obsidian Butterfly never manage to reach the level this one seems to effortlessly float to.</span>

<div id="review_731507800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/731507800" />
    <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire"><img alt="Beth The Vampire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483516030p2/22241496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/731507800?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth The Vampire" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire">Beth The Vampire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755355372" href="/book/show/7042657-obsidian-butterfly">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=series-6-to-10">series-6-to-10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer731507800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9344607917081987067"><b>ACTUAL RATING 3.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>In one sense this was a big step up for the Anita Blake series, but on the other hand there were still a few things that irked me.<br/><br/>So this book, the 9th in the series, actually had a plot. Shock horror. The last few had some semblance of a plot, but not much, and the story so diverged from that at times it was beyond frustrating. This time Anita is called to help friend, monster hunter, and downright psychopath, Edward, after a case comes his way that seems to terrify even </span>
  <span id="freeText9344607917081987067" style="display:none"><b>ACTUAL RATING 3.5 STARS</b><br /><br />In one sense this was a big step up for the Anita Blake series, but on the other hand there were still a few things that irked me.<br /><br />So this book, the 9th in the series, actually had a plot. Shock horror. The last few had some semblance of a plot, but not much, and the story so diverged from that at times it was beyond frustrating. This time Anita is called to help friend, monster hunter, and downright psychopath, Edward, after a case comes his way that seems to terrify even him. People are being mutilated, torn into shreds, and then some are skinned and left alive. No one knows who, are more likely what, is carrying out these horrific crimes, but Edwards has his own band of rag tags to help solve what the police cannot. Bernardo and Olaf (who I couldn’t help imagining as a snowman….a murdering rapist snowman), are along for the ride, but Edwards is hoping that Anita can spot what they cannot. Add in some issues around Edwards new finance and stepkids, and Anita trying to deal with cutting off her links to her two boyfriends, and we have a story.<br /><br />This book was heading towards four stars until….child abuse. Of course the stepkids were going to get captured. But why not just have them locked in separate rooms? Why not have them bound and gagged and left on the floor? Why we had to witness actual child abuse for two whole pages was beyond me. It was not necessary at all and frankly disturbed me a lot. Those kids are going to be fucked up. I’m a social worker, I deal with traumatised kids every second of every day and let me tell you, those kids are not going to be okay. At the end, Anita was just telling them to see a therapist, to talk about the issues, and then they were just forgotten. No. Nope. No fucking way. Why was this even necessary, and to describe it in such detail. For me, it was just not great, and really ruined the rest of the book. I scanned the next few chapters, not really caring what happened, because I was just done.<br /><br />When I really think about it, these books are really becoming pro-murder. Anita feels threatened by Olaf, the rapist who likes to cut apart his victims, but he saved her life, so he’s okay. Sure, let’s just let him go on a killing spree because it’s how he gets his jollies. At multiple times in this book Anita goes through how many people/monsters she has killed, and even though she doesn’t feel proud of it, she is. It’s a badge of honour for her. Anita tries to be one God, magnanimous, and pro life, but I feel she may have some kind of identity disorder because what she does and what she thinks are two different things. Sometimes I think she has empathy, but then she proves she’s just another blank murdering slate. There’s just so much unnecessary murder in these books. How much further can Anita go down the psychopath hole before there is no coming back? I’m not even interested, but if this series goes on for 22+ books, then she is soon going to become some kind of emotionless killer, if she’s not there already.<br /><br />So this book gets three stars for having a plot (because I have to be encouraging don’t I?) and for a while being interesting before we added murder and sex into the equation. And it loses half a star for the unnecessary rape and physically assault of two children, and then just brushing it off thinking they will be fine in the end. And half a star is being generous. The ending was quite abrupt, and really not as horrific as the actual crimes, and the last few pages is dedicated to Anita pausing over he love life, instead of actually reflecting on what she has learned from her experiences and how it has affected her. In the end, it really didn’t matter. And I think that proves how heartless Anita really is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9344607917081987067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fwfFiJ367AtXdj4EDn8MsfVI/tL6yxJvqzzqtZWxQQ/vNyLNdO7Pq4fa4wAeJx0JeW+C3RONAhpyYWAs3yBZWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ijgwjYRe378MQJq8u8K19XDbOIN1WzcoT0u4U93cV7waCNfIbUr8H9zsR7irmqRN/PxEjJwdJ12WFjLKl01P6g==')})
  }
